## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: continuum mechanics / constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship of a material, which is a fundamental constitutive relation in materials science. Temperature typically causes thermal softening while strain causes hardening, and their interplay determines the mechanical response.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elastic stress-strain at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (1 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with thermal softening of modulus)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (Hollomon equation for strain hardening)
- Ludwik equation: sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (elastic-plastic with yield stress and power hardening)
- Ramberg-Osgood type: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combined linear and nonlinear strain terms)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 - c1 * exp(c2 * epsilon) (saturation hardening model)
- Johnson-Cook strength model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 + c3 * T) (combined hardening and thermal softening)
- Thermal softening power law: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (thermally activated softening with hardening)
- Johnson-Cook thermal term: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (hardening with exponential thermal softening)
- Swift-type law: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 (shifted power-law hardening avoiding singularity at zero strain)
- Zener-Hollomon inspired: sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon * exp(c2 * T)) (hyperbolic sine flow stress model)
- Linear thermal + Voce: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (saturation stress with thermal dependence)
- Polynomial hardening with thermal coupling: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) * (1 + c3 * T) (quadratic hardening with linear thermal factor)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Strain hardening (concave-down stress-strain curve) → Power-law epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1, or saturation form (1 - exp(-c*epsilon))
- Thermal softening (stress decreases with temperature) → Multiplicative factor (1 - c*T**n), exp(-c*T), or T**(-c)
- Yield stress offset (nonzero stress intercept at small strain) → Additive constant c0 + f(epsilon), or shifted power law (epsilon + c)**n
- Saturation stress at large strains → Exponential approach to limit: c0*(1 - exp(-c1*epsilon)), or rational form epsilon/(epsilon + c)
- Thermally-activated deformation (Arrhenius-type mechanism) → sinh or asinh functions of strain rate/strain scaled by exp(c/T)
- Separable vs coupled strain-temperature effects → Multiplicative separation f(epsilon)*g(T) vs additive f(epsilon) + g(T) vs coupled f(epsilon, T)
- Phase transition or abrupt softening at critical temperature → Sigmoidal temperature dependence, tanh((T - Tc)*c)
- Elastic-to-plastic transition → Piecewise-like behavior approximated by smooth functions: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 with c2 < 1
